5. Query Optimization Recommendations
Six highest-impact query optimization opportunities identified. Each includes the current problematic pattern and the optimized replacement with quantified improvement estimates.
Dashboard Net Worth — 8 Separate Aggregate Queries
PROB
Dashboard fires 8 individual SUM/COUNT queries sequentially on different tables. At 1M users with 100k concurrent sessions, this generates 800k DB queries per second from dashboard alone.
Current Pattern:
SELECT SUM(amount) FROM income_entries WHERE user_id=?
SELECT SUM(amount) FROM expenses WHERE user_id=?
SELECT SUM(current_value) FROM investments WHERE user_id=?
SELECT SUM(outstanding_amount) FROM debts WHERE user_id=?
... (4 more queries)
Optimized Pattern:
-- Primary: read from Redis cache (TTL 15 min)
GET dashboard:user:{id}:summary
-- Cache miss: read from financial_snapshots
SELECT * FROM financial_snapshots
WHERE user_id=? ORDER BY year DESC, month DESC LIMIT 1
-- Then add current-month delta (2 queries total)
WIN
From 8 queries x 100k users = 800k queries/sec DOWN TO 2 queries + Redis lookup
Expense Category Budget Check on Every Save
PROB
On every expense INSERT, the system must check current month's total for that category vs the budget. With 1M users saving 30 expenses/day = 30M budget checks/day.
Current Pattern:
SELECT SUM(amount) FROM expenses
WHERE user_id=? AND expense_category_id=?
AND MONTH(expense_date)=? AND YEAR(expense_date)=?
Optimized Pattern:
-- After normalization fix (remove month/year columns), use index:
-- Index: idx_exp_user_cat_date on (user_id, expense_category_id, expense_date)
SELECT SUM(amount) FROM expenses
WHERE user_id=? AND expense_category_id=?
AND expense_date BETWEEN 2026-06-01 AND 2026-06-30
-- Covering index: no heap lookup needed
WIN
Full table scan elimination. Index range scan on (user_id, category_id, date) — microseconds not seconds
XIRR Computation Reads All Investment Transactions
PROB
XIRR requires all transaction history per investment in date order. A user with 5-year SIP has 60+ rows. Platform-wide XIRR computation at 1M users = 1M+ queries.
Current Pattern:
-- Runs synchronously on every portfolio view
SELECT amount, transaction_date FROM investment_transactions
WHERE investment_id=? ORDER BY transaction_date ASC
-- Then Newton-Raphson in PHP — blocking request
Optimized Pattern:
-- Async nightly job only:
SELECT amount, transaction_date FROM investment_transactions
WHERE investment_id=? ORDER BY transaction_date ASC
-- Index: idx_it_inv_date on (investment_id, transaction_date)
-- Batch: process 1000 investments per job worker
-- Write result: UPDATE investments SET xirr=?, last_computed_at=NOW()
-- API reads stored xirr_percentage — no compute on request
WIN
Eliminates XIRR compute from request path entirely. Nightly batch job runs off-peak.
Report Generation — Unpartitioned Table Full Scans
PROB
Yearly report runs GROUP BY on income_entries and expenses tables. At 1M users x 30 expenses/month x 12 months = 360M rows in expenses. Full table scan takes 30-90 seconds.
Current Pattern:
SELECT category_id, SUM(amount) FROM expenses
WHERE user_id=? AND YEAR(expense_date)=2025
GROUP BY expense_category_id
-- YEAR() function on expense_date disables index use
Optimized Pattern:
-- After partitioning by year:
-- Partition pruning selects only p2025 partition
SELECT category_id, SUM(amount) FROM expenses PARTITION (p2025)
WHERE user_id=? AND expense_date BETWEEN 2025-01-01 AND 2025-12-31
GROUP BY expense_category_id
-- No function on indexed column — index used for user_id+date range
WIN
Partition pruning reduces scan from 360M rows to ~36M rows (1 year partition). 10x improvement.
Audit Log Compliance Query — No Functional Index on JSON
PROB
Regulators ask: "Show all changes where amount exceeded Rs.1,00,000". Must search JSON new_values blob across 500M audit rows.
Current Pattern:
SELECT * FROM audit_logs
WHERE JSON_UNQUOTE(JSON_EXTRACT(new_values, "$.amount")) > 100000
-- Full table scan — no index on JSON extract
Optimized Pattern:
-- Add functional index on critical JSON fields:
ALTER TABLE audit_logs ADD INDEX idx_aud_amount
  ((CAST(JSON_UNQUOTE(JSON_EXTRACT(new_values, "$.amount")) AS DECIMAL(15,2))));
-- Or: add amount column to audit_logs for frequently queried fields
ALTER TABLE audit_logs ADD COLUMN change_amount DECIMAL(15,2) NULL;
-- Populate on INSERT. Index: idx_aud_change_amount
WIN
Eliminates full table scan on 500M-row table. Compliance queries from minutes to milliseconds.
Goal Progress Calculation Uses Stored current_amount (Drift Risk)
PROB
financial_goals.current_amount is stored and updated on each contribution. If a contribution is soft-deleted, current_amount does not auto-correct. This is a data consistency bug not just a performance issue.
Current Pattern:
-- Current: read stale stored value
SELECT current_amount, target_amount FROM financial_goals WHERE id=?
-- Potentially wrong if contributions were deleted
Optimized Pattern:
-- Option 1: Derive from contributions (accurate, slightly slower)
SELECT COALESCE(SUM(amount),0) AS current_amount
FROM goal_contributions
WHERE financial_goal_id=? AND deleted_at IS NULL
-- Option 2: Nightly reconciliation job corrects stored value
UPDATE financial_goals fg SET current_amount = (
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(gc.amount),0) FROM goal_contributions gc
  WHERE gc.financial_goal_id=fg.id AND gc.deleted_at IS NULL
) WHERE fg.deleted_at IS NULL
WIN
Data accuracy fix. Reconciliation job runs nightly. API reads corrected stored value for performance.
5.7 General Query Rules
Never use functions on indexed columns in WHERE: YEAR(date)=? disables index. Use date BETWEEN start AND end.
Always use LIMIT on user-facing queries. No unbounded SELECT * without pagination.
Use EXPLAIN ANALYZE (MySQL 8.0+) on every new query before deploying to production.
Use SELECT only needed columns — never SELECT * in application code. Reduces network and buffer pool usage.
Batch INSERT over multiple single INSERTs. Audit log writes should be queued and batch-inserted in groups of 100.
Use READ UNCOMMITTED isolation for dashboard cache-warming jobs. No dirty data risk for aggregate snapshots.
6. Partitioning Recommendations
10 tables require partitioning before the platform reaches 100,000 users. At 1 million users, unpartitioned tables for expenses, audit_logs, and income_entries will have hundreds of millions of rows — making report queries and compliance searches unacceptably slow.
Table
Partition Strategy
Partition Definitions
Priority
Justification
expenses
RANGE on YEAR(expense_date)
p2024 (2024), p2025 (2025), p2026 (2026), p_future (MAXVALUE)
CRITICAL
Largest table. 1M users x 360 expenses/year = 360M rows in 5 years. Partition pruning reduces yearly report scans by 80%.
income_entries
RANGE on YEAR(income_date)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
HIGH
Report queries always specify year. Pruning essential for performance.
investment_transactions
RANGE on YEAR(transaction_date)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
HIGH
XIRR computation reads all rows. Partition by year limits read scope for newer investors.
audit_logs
RANGE on YEAR(created_at)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
CRITICAL
Fastest growing table. No business query ever needs all years. Compliance queries always specify date range.
debt_payments
RANGE on YEAR(payment_date)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
MEDIUM
Home loan payments over 20 years = 240 rows/loan. At 100k loans: 24M rows. Partition keeps per-year queries fast.
login_events
RANGE on YEAR(created_at)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
HIGH
Security audit queries always recent (last 90 days). Old partitions archived, dropped.
notifications
RANGE on YEAR(created_at)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
MEDIUM
Old notifications deleted after 1 year. Partition makes cleanup an O(1) partition drop.
financial_snapshots
RANGE on YEAR(snapshot_date)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
LOW
Only 12 rows/user/year. But grows with users. Partition future-proofs the table.
idempotency_keys
RANGE on YEAR(created_at)
p_current (rolling 2-month window)
MEDIUM
Keys expire in 24h. Use partition for fast cleanup: DROP PARTITION p_old instead of mass DELETE.
exchange_rates
RANGE on YEAR(rate_date)
p2024, p2025, p2026, p_future
LOW
Historical rates kept for re-calculation. Partition separates current vs historical rates cleanly.
6.1 Partition Management Rules
Create new year partitions automatically via a scheduled job that runs every December 1st.
Never perform ALTER TABLE ADD PARTITION on a table with active concurrent writes — schedule during maintenance window.
Use pt-online-schema-change (Percona Toolkit) for zero-downtime partition additions on tables > 10M rows.
Partition pruning only works when the WHERE clause uses the partition key column directly — no functions (no YEAR(date)).
Test partition pruning with EXPLAIN PARTITIONS: verify "partitions" column shows only the expected partition(s).
Global indexes (non-partition-local) are not supported in MySQL range partitioning — all indexes must be local or include partition key.
6.2 Sub-Partitioning Strategy (100k+ Users)
ADV
Sub-partition expenses by HASH(user_id % 16) within each year partition.
This creates 16 sub-partitions per year — each handling ~62,500 users at 1M scale.
Benefit: concurrent DML on different sub-partitions avoids contention. Useful when write throughput > 50k/sec.
Trade-off: 16x more partition metadata overhead. Only implement when single-partition write contention is measured.
7. Archive Strategy
A four-tier data lifecycle architecture manages data from hot production storage through to compliance-grade frozen archives. The strategy reduces primary database size by 70-85% within 4 years of operation at scale.
7.1 Storage Tier Definitions
Tier
Storage
Age Range
Characteristics
HOT
MySQL InnoDB (Primary)
0 — 24 months
All active data. Full read/write. Full index coverage. InnoDB buffer pool.
WARM
MySQL Read Replica
24 — 48 months
Historical queries. Read-only. Same schema. Auto-sync from primary via binlog.
COLD
S3 Parquet (Apache Parquet format)
48+ months
Archive storage. Query via AWS Athena SQL. Pay per query. Cost: ~$5/TB/month.
FROZEN
S3 Glacier Deep Archive
7+ years
Compliance retention only. Retrieval time: 12-48 hours. Cost: ~$1/TB/month.
7.2 Per-Table Archive Schedule
Table
HOT (MySQL)
WARM (Replica)
COLD (S3 Parquet)
Retention
expenses
Active: 24 months in MySQL
Warm: 24-48 months on read replica
Cold: 48+ months in S3 Parquet
7 years (DPDP)
income_entries
Active: 24 months
Warm: 24-48 months
Cold: 48+ months
7 years
audit_logs
Active: 12 months
Warm: 12-36 months
Cold: 36+ months
10 years (financial regulation)
investment_transactions
Active: 36 months (XIRR needs history)
Warm: 36-60 months
Cold: 60+ months
10 years (capital gains)
debt_payments
Active: Full loan life
Warm: 24 months post-close
Cold: Post-closure
7 years
login_events
Active: 3 months
Warm: 3-12 months
Cold: 12-36 months
3 years (security)
notifications
Active: 3 months (auto-delete after read)
—
Archive: 3-12 months
1 year
ledger_entries
NEVER archive primary
Warm replica: always
Cold: 7+ years
Permanent (financial records)
7.3 Archival Job Specification
Job name: ArchiveOldTransactions — runs 1st of each month at 02:00 IST (off-peak)
Step 1: SELECT rows WHERE partition_date < cutoff_date into S3 via Apache Arrow / DuckDB export
Step 2: Compress to Parquet format with Snappy compression (typically 80% size reduction vs CSV)
Step 3: Write to S3 path: s3://ffp-archive/{table}/{year}/{month}/data.parquet
Step 4: Register Parquet files in AWS Glue Data Catalog for Athena queryability
Step 5: INSERT metadata into archived_transaction_meta table (table, original_id range, s3_path)
Step 6: DROP the MySQL partition for archived data (instant, no row-by-row DELETE)
Step 7: Send completion report to admin email with row count, S3 size, partition freed
WARN
DPDP Right to Erasure applies to archived data too. When a user requests deletion:
  1. Delete from MySQL (hot/warm) immediately.
  2. Submit S3 Object Tagging job to mark archived objects for deletion within 30 days.
  3. AWS S3 Lifecycle policy processes deletion tags within configured SLA.
  4. Record deletion completion in data_deletion_requests.completed_at.
Parquet is columnar — user_id filtering on S3 uses Parquet predicate pushdown to avoid full file reads.
8. Backup Strategy
A multi-layer backup strategy covering RTO/RPO targets, automated snapshots, binary log streaming, cross-region replication, and compliance-grade long-term retention. All backups encrypted at rest with AWS KMS.
8.1 SLA Targets
Metric
Target
How Achieved
RTO (Recovery Time Objective)
15 minutes
Time to restore service after failure. Achieved via RDS Multi-AZ automatic failover.
RPO (Recovery Point Objective)
< 1 minute
Maximum data loss. Achieved via binlog streaming to S3 with 60-second flush interval.
Full Backup Frequency
Daily at 01:00 IST
Automated RDS snapshot or mysqldump on non-primary replica.
Incremental Backup
Every 5 minutes
Binary log (binlog) streaming to S3. Enables Point-In-Time Recovery (PITR).
PITR Window
35 days
Can restore to any second in the past 35 days.
Cross-Region Replication
ap-south-1 -> ap-southeast-1
Mumbai primary, Singapore disaster recovery replica.
Backup Retention (Hot)
35 days on S3 Standard
Recent backups for fast restore.
Backup Retention (Cold)
7 years on S3 Glacier
Compliance archive. Encrypted with AES-256.
Encryption
AES-256 at rest + TLS 1.3 in transit
AWS KMS managed keys. Key rotation every 365 days.
Backup Testing
Monthly restore test on isolated environment
Verify backup integrity and RTO achievement. Document results.
8.2 Backup Type Matrix
Type
What Is Backed Up
Frequency
Trade-offs
Logical Backup (mysqldump)
Full schema + data in SQL format
Daily on dev/staging
Human-readable, portable across MySQL versions, slow for large tables
Physical Backup (xtrabackup)
Raw InnoDB files
Daily on production
Fast restore, exact byte copy, requires same MySQL version
RDS Automated Snapshots
AWS-managed EBS snapshot
Daily (AWS managed)
One-click restore in AWS Console, no maintenance required
Binlog Streaming
Incremental changes as binary log events
Continuous to S3
Enables PITR, used for read replica sync, smallest RPO
Read Replica
Live standby with real-time data
Always-on
Zero restore time for read queries. 30-60 second lag for PITR writes.
Cross-Region Copy
Encrypted backup copied to DR region
Every 6 hours
Regional disaster recovery. Higher S3 data transfer cost.
8.3 Backup Testing Protocol
Monthly: Restore last daily snapshot to isolated test environment. Verify row counts match production for 5 sampled tables.
Quarterly: Full disaster recovery drill. Failover to cross-region replica. Verify application connects and serves traffic.
Annually: PITR test — restore to a specific timestamp 7 days in the past. Validate data consistency vs expected state.
Backup monitoring: Alert if backup job fails or backup age exceeds RPO threshold. PagerDuty integration.
Encryption validation: Monthly verify backup files are encrypted. Attempt decryption without KMS key — must fail.
9. Data Retention Policy
Retention periods governed by India's DPDP Act 2023, the Income Tax Act, and RBI fintech guidelines. Financial records have longer retention requirements than most SaaS applications. Retention periods are enforced by automated purge jobs and S3 lifecycle policies.
Table / Data
Retention Period
Legal Basis
users
Account active: indefinitely. After deletion request: 30 days then purge
DPDP Act: data held only as long as purpose exists. 30-day grace allows cancellation.
income_entries
7 years after entry date
Income tax records required for 7 years per Indian IT Act Section 149.
expenses
7 years after entry date
Business expense proof retention per Indian IT Act. Personal: 5 years minimum.
audit_logs
10 years from creation
RBI/SEBI fintech regulations require 10-year audit trail. Never purged — archived to Glacier.
investment_transactions
10 years from transaction date
Capital gains computation may require lookback for LTCG (held > 1 year at time of sale).
debt_payments
7 years after debt closure
Loan repayment proof for future loan applications and income tax purposes.
ledger_entries
Permanent — never deleted
Ledger is the financial record of truth. Permanent retention even after account closure.
login_events
3 years from event date
Security audit requirement. Anomaly detection lookback rarely exceeds 90 days.
notifications
1 year from creation
No regulatory requirement. User-facing history window. Old notifications auto-pruned.
idempotency_keys
24 hours from creation
Technical deduplication only. Expired keys purged nightly.
trusted_devices
2 years from last_seen, or on revocation
Security: old trusted devices should require re-verification.
consent_records
Permanent — never deleted
DPDP requires consent history to be demonstrable at any future audit.
financial_snapshots
10 years from snapshot_date
Net worth history has long-term value. Tax planning and financial planning lookback.
exchange_rates
7 years from rate_date
Historical rates needed for re-calculation of old multi-currency transactions.
file_uploads (S3)
7 years for financial receipts. 1 year for avatars
Receipts are financial documents. Avatars are non-essential.
data_deletion_requests
Permanent record of request + completion
DPDP requires proof of honoring deletion requests even after data is deleted.
9.1 Automated Purge Jobs
Daily Purge Job: DELETE FROM notifications WHERE created_at < NOW() - INTERVAL 1 YEAR AND read_at IS NOT NULL
Daily Purge Job: DELETE FROM idempotency_keys WHERE expires_at < NOW()
Daily Purge Job: DELETE FROM login_events WHERE created_at < NOW() - INTERVAL 3 YEAR
Monthly Archival Job: Move expenses, income_entries older than 24 months to S3 Parquet (Section 7)
Monthly Purge: DELETE soft-deleted records WHERE deleted_at < NOW() - INTERVAL 90 DAY (except ledger_entries — never)
Annual Glacier Migration: Move S3 Standard archives older than 4 years to S3 Glacier Deep Archive
9.2 User-Triggered Deletion (DPDP Right to Erasure)
Step 1: Receive POST /me/request-deletion. Create data_deletion_requests record. Schedule 30 days out.
Step 2: Day 0-30: User can cancel deletion by logging in. Show cancellation option prominently.
Step 3: Day 30: Automated job soft-deletes all user-owned records (users, expenses, income, goals, etc.)
Step 4: Day 30: Tag all user S3 objects for deletion. AWS Lifecycle policy processes within 48 hours.
Step 5: Day 90: Hard-delete soft-deleted records from MySQL (partition drop for large tables if possible).
Step 6: Exception: ledger_entries, consent_records, data_deletion_requests are anonymized but never deleted.
Step 7: Update data_deletion_requests.status=completed, completed_at=NOW(). Email confirmation to last known address.
10. Scalability — 1 Million Users
Detailed projections for data volumes, infrastructure sizing, CQRS architecture, and horizontal sharding strategy to support 1 million active users with <500ms dashboard response times.
10.1 Data Volume Projections at 1M Users
Metric
Volume
Assumptions
Total Rows — expenses
360M
1M users x 360 expenses/year x avg 1 year history
Total Rows — income_entries
24M
1M users x 24 income entries/year
Total Rows — audit_logs
500M+
1M users x ~500 auditable actions/year across all modules
Total Rows — investment_transactions
60M
500k investors x avg 120 transactions/year (SIPs)
Total Rows — debt_payments
24M
200k debtors x avg 120 payments over loan life
Total Rows — notifications
300M
1M users x 300 notifications/year (before pruning)
Total Rows — login_events
730M
1M users x 730 logins/year (2/day avg)
Peak DB Writes/sec
50,000
Evening peak: expenses, income entries, goal contributions
Peak DB Reads/sec
500,000
Dashboard loads: 1M users x 10% DAU x 10 reads/session
Total DB Storage
15-20 TB
Including indexes, partitions. Before archival.
Redis Memory
64-128 GB
Dashboard caches, session tokens, idempotency keys, rate limits
S3 Archive Storage
50-100 TB/year
Parquet archives. At $23/TB/month = ~$1,150-$2,300/month
10.2 Infrastructure Architecture
Component
Specification
Primary MySQL (RDS)
Write endpoint. Multi-AZ. db.r6g.8xlarge (32 vCPU, 256GB RAM). io2 SSD 10,000 IOPS.
Read Replicas (x3)
Separate read endpoint. Report queries, dashboard misses, analytics. Same instance class.
Redis Cluster (ElastiCache)
6-node cluster (3 primary + 3 replica). cache.r6g.4xlarge. 128GB RAM per node.
Connection Pooling (ProxySQL)
Sit between app and MySQL. Pool 10,000 app connections into 500 DB connections.
Application Servers
Auto-scaling group. 20-100 Laravel Octane instances (Swoole). Behind ALB.
Queue Workers (Horizon)
50-200 workers. Separate ASG. Handle report generation, XIRR jobs, notifications.
S3 + CloudFront
Static assets, exported reports, file uploads. CloudFront CDN for download speed.
AWS Athena
Query archived Parquet data on S3. Ad-hoc compliance queries without impacting MySQL.
10.3 CQRS Architecture
Pattern
Implementation
Command Side (Write)
Single Primary MySQL. All INSERTs, UPDATEs, DELETEs. Synchronous. Ledger integrity enforced here.
Query Side (Read)
3 Read Replicas + Redis. Dashboard, reports, lists. Eventual consistency (30-60 sec lag) acceptable for aggregates.
Event Sourcing (Optional V3)
Replace UPDATE-in-place with append-only event stream. Full audit trail without separate audit_logs table. AWS QLDB.
Cache Invalidation
Write events published to Redis pub/sub. Cache consumers invalidate relevant keys on data change.
Denormalized Read Models
financial_snapshots, expense_trends, financial_health_scores are query-side read models refreshed by scheduled jobs.
10.4 Horizontal Sharding Strategy (5M+ Users)
Aspect
Design Decision
Approach
Horizontal sharding by tenant_id (for enterprise) or user_id range (for consumer)
Shard Key
tenant_id for B2B tier. SHA-256(user_id) % N for consumer tier.
Shard Count
Start with 4 shards. Double to 8 at 2M users. Double to 16 at 5M users.
Cross-Shard Queries
Prohibited. Aggregations (platform stats) run on a separate analytics replica.
Shard Routing
Application-level: middleware looks up shard from tenant/user shard map in Redis.
Resharding
Use Vitess (YouTube's MySQL sharding framework) for live resharding without downtime.
10.5 Scaling Milestones
User Count
Action Required
Timeline
0 — 10,000
Baseline schema. Single MySQL. Redis. No partitioning needed yet.
Months 1-12
10,000 — 100,000
Add 1 read replica. Implement Redis dashboard cache. Add all indexes.
Months 12-24
100,000 — 250,000
Implement table partitioning (Section 6). Add ProxySQL connection pooling.
Months 24-36
250,000 — 500,000
Add 2 more read replicas. Implement archival jobs. Upgrade RDS instance class.
Months 36-48
500,000 — 1,000,000
Full CQRS separation. Begin Vitess evaluation. CloudFront for S3 downloads.
Months 48-60
1,000,000+
Horizontal sharding via Vitess. Schema-per-tenant for enterprise. Global Athena analytics.
60+ months
11. Optimized DBML Schema
Complete DBML v2.0 with all architectural improvements applied: ENUM removal, derived column elimination, tenant isolation, ledger tables, lookup tables, encryption columns, and full index definitions. Paste into dbdiagram.io to render interactive ER diagram.
USE
Copy the DBML text below and paste at https://dbdiagram.io to generate a fully interactive ER diagram.
The schema includes all 53 tables with relationships, indexes, and inline notes.
DBML ref syntax: [ref: > table.column] means many-to-one (FK references). [ref: <> ] means many-to-many.
// Financial Freedom Planner — Optimized DBML v2.0
// Improvements: removed derived month/year columns, replaced ENUMs with FK lookups,
// added tenant_id, ledger tables, encryption key versioning, all indexes defined.
Table tenants {
  id uuid [pk, note: "UUID v4 — public-safe tenant identifier"]
  name varchar(100) [not null]
  slug varchar(120) [unique, not null, note: "subdomain key e.g. acme for acme.ffplanner.in"]
  plan_id bigint [ref: > subscription_plans.id, null]
  settings json [note: "feature flags, white-label config"]
  is_active tinyint [default: 1]
  created_at timestamp
  updated_at timestamp
  indexes { slug [unique] }
}

  id bigint [pk, increment]
  name varchar(100) [not null]
  slug varchar(120) [unique]
  price_monthly decimal(10,2) [default: 0]
  price_yearly decimal(10,2) [default: 0]
  features json
  is_active tinyint [default: 1]
  created_at timestamp
  updated_at timestamp
}
Table users {
  id bigint [pk, increment]
  ulid char(26) [unique, not null, note: "Public-facing identifier — prevents ID enumeration"]
  tenant_id uuid [ref: > tenants.id, not null, note: "Multi-tenancy partition key"]
  name varchar(100) [not null]
  email varchar(150) [unique, not null]
  email_verified_at timestamp [null]
  password varchar(255) [not null, note: "bcrypt hash, never plain text"]
  phone varchar(20) [null]
  avatar varchar(500) [null, note: "S3 key only — URL generated on demand via signed URL"]
  subscription_plan_id bigint [ref: > subscription_plans.id, null]
  parent_user_id bigint [ref: > users.id, null, note: "v2: family account head"]
  two_factor_secret text [null, note: "AES encrypted TOTP secret"]
  two_factor_recovery_codes text [null, note: "Encrypted JSON array"]
  account_locked_until timestamp [null]
  failed_login_count tinyint [default: 0]
  last_login_at timestamp [null]
  privacy_policy_version_id bigint [ref: > privacy_policy_versions.id, null]
  is_active tinyint [default: 1]
  remember_token varchar(100) [null]
  deleted_at timestamp [null]
  created_at timestamp
  updated_at timestamp
  indexes {
    email [unique]
    tenant_id
    deleted_at
    subscription_plan_id
    (tenant_id, is_active)
  }
}

  name varchar(200) [not null]
  target_amount decimal(15,4) [not null]
  current_amount decimal(15,4) [default: 0, note: "Denorm. Source: SUM(goal_contributions). Reconciled nightly."]
  adjusted_target_amount decimal(15,4) [null, note: "Inflation-adjusted target. Recomputed monthly by scheduler."]
  target_date date [not null]
  inflation_rate decimal(5,2) [default: 6.00]
  expected_return_rate decimal(5,2) [default: 0.00]
  priority tinyint [default: 2, note: "1=High 2=Medium 3=Low"]
  monthly_allocation decimal(15,4) [null]
  status varchar(20) [default: "active", note: "active|completed|paused|cancelled"]
  notes text [null]
  deleted_at timestamp [null]
  created_at timestamp
  updated_at timestamp
  indexes {
    user_id
    (user_id, status, priority)
    (user_id, target_date)
    (tenant_id, user_id)
  }
}

  amount decimal(15,4) [not null]
  contribution_date date [not null]
  notes text [null]
  deleted_at timestamp [null]
  created_at timestamp
  updated_at timestamp
  indexes { financial_goal_id; (financial_goal_id, contribution_date) }
}

Table ledger_entries {
  id bigint [pk, increment]

  note: "APPEND-ONLY. Never UPDATE or DELETE. Permanent financial record."
  indexes {
    ledger_account_id
    (user_id, posted_at)
    (transaction_ref_type, transaction_ref_id)
    (tenant_id, user_id, posted_at)
  }
}

  new_values json [null]

  user_agent text [null]
  created_at timestamp [not null]
  note: "PARTITION BY RANGE (YEAR(created_at)). INSERT-ONLY — no UPDATE or DELETE permitted."
  indexes {
    user_id

  }

12. ER Diagram Notes
12.1 Entity Group Map
The 53 tables organize into 11 logical groups. Understanding group boundaries helps identify correct JOIN paths and avoids cross-group coupling.
Group
Tables
Design Notes
Core Identity Group
users, tenants, roles, permissions, role_user, permission_role, user_preferences, subscription_plans
Central cluster. Every other table references users.id. tenant_id creates the multi-tenancy boundary. user_preferences separates account from preference attributes (3NF compliance).
Income Group
salary_sources, income_entries, income_source_types
1:Many chain: user -> salary_sources -> income_entries. income_source_types is a lookup (replaces ENUM). income_entries connects to ledger_entries via transaction_ref.
Expense Group
expense_categories, expenses, expense_budgets, expense_trends
expense_categories can be system (user_id=NULL) or user-owned. expenses references categories. expense_budgets is a (user, category, month, year) keyed control table. expense_trends is a denormalized read model.
Savings Group
saving_accounts, saving_transactions, saving_bucket_types, goal_milestones
1:Many: saving_accounts -> saving_transactions. saving_bucket_types replaces ENUM. current_amount on saving_accounts is a derived denorm.
Goals Group
financial_goals, goal_contributions, goal_projections, goal_type_lookup
1:Many: financial_goals -> goal_contributions. goal_projections stores TVM scenario results. current_amount derives from goal_contributions aggregate.
Investment Group
investment_types, investments, investment_transactions, sip_schedules, investment_benchmarks
investment_types is admin-managed master data. 1:Many: investments -> investment_transactions. sip_schedules manages recurring SIP automation. xirr_percentage is nightly-computed denorm.
Debt Group
debts, debt_amortization_schedule, debt_payments, debt_rate_changes, debt_type_lookup, payment_modes
Most complex group. debts -> amortization_schedule (1:Many, regenerated on changes). debt_rate_changes tracks floating rate history. debt_type_lookup and payment_modes replace ENUMs.
Double-Entry Ledger Group
ledger_accounts, ledger_entries
Foundational integrity layer. Every money movement in any module creates two ledger_entries (debit + credit). ledger_accounts holds running balances. APPEND-ONLY — no updates or deletes ever.
Analytics Group (Read Models)
financial_snapshots, expense_trends, financial_health_scores, tax_summaries
All denormalized. Written by scheduled background jobs. Read by dashboard and reports. Source of truth is always the normalized transactional tables. Never written to by user-facing APIs.
Security & Compliance Group
audit_logs, login_events, trusted_devices, idempotency_keys, consent_records, data_deletion_requests, privacy_policy_versions, encryption_key_versions
Compliance infrastructure. audit_logs is hash-chained and INSERT-only. consent_records and data_deletion_requests are permanent (never deleted per DPDP). encryption_key_versions tracks AES key rotation.
File & Utility Group
file_uploads, exchange_rates, notifications, device_tokens, emergency_funds
Supporting tables. file_uploads stores S3 keys only (never full URLs). exchange_rates has historical rate data. emergency_funds is 1:1 with users.
12.2 Key Design Decisions
Decision
Rationale
All PKs are BIGINT UNSIGNED AUTO_INCREMENT
Consistent, InnoDB-friendly clustered index. BIGINT gives 9.2 quintillion rows before overflow.
All public IDs use ULID (CHAR 26)
Prevents ID enumeration attacks. Lexicographically sortable unlike UUID. Used in all API routes.
tenant_id UUID on all user-data tables
First column in composite indexes. Creates hard tenant boundary. Enables future schema-per-tenant migration.
All monetary amounts: DECIMAL(15,4)
4 decimal places for BCMath intermediate precision. Display rounds to 2. Never use FLOAT or DOUBLE for money.
Sensitive columns use encrypted cast
AES-256-GCM via Laravel encrypted cast. Stored as TEXT (ciphertext). Cannot be SUM()ed in SQL.
Soft deletes: deleted_at TIMESTAMP NULL
All user-data tables. Hard deletes via purge job after 90-day grace. Ledger_entries: never soft-deleted.
created_at + updated_at on all tables
Standard Eloquent timestamps. Used for delta sync (mobile offline support) and cache invalidation.
financial_year CHAR(7) on transaction tables
Indian financial year (April-March). e.g. "2025-26". Eliminates complex date arithmetic for ITR queries.
JSON columns for flexible metadata
settings (tenants), features (plans), data (notifications), old/new_values (audit_logs). Avoid over-normalizing infrequently queried metadata.
APPEND-ONLY constraint on ledger_entries
No UPDATE or DELETE. DB user has INSERT-only permission on this table. Enforces financial integrity at infrastructure level.
12.3 Critical Relationship Rules
One user ALWAYS belongs to one tenant. Cross-tenant user relationships are prohibited.
Every financial transaction (income, expense, saving, investment, debt payment) MUST create a ledger_entries pair.
expense_categories with user_id=NULL are system-owned. Users cannot delete them but can use them.
financial_goals.current_amount and saving_accounts.current_amount are denormalized caches — they must match their respective aggregate sources at all times.
audit_logs.previous_hash links to the previous row's row_hash — forming a tamper-evident chain. The chain must be verifiable.
ledger_entries has NO foreign key to the source transaction tables — uses transaction_ref_type + transaction_ref_id polymorphic pattern.
13. Migration Order
58 migrations in strict dependency order. Run php artisan migrate from top to bottom. Migrations 001-015 must complete before any user-data table migration begins.
RULE
Rule 1: Never create a table before its FK dependencies exist. Follow this exact order.
Rule 2: Partition migrations (058) run LAST — tables must exist before partitioning.
Rule 3: Index migrations (056, 057) run after all tables are created — not during table creation.
Rule 4: Lookup table seeders run BEFORE feature seeders (system categories, investment types need IDs first).

14. Seeder Strategy
23 seeders organized in strict dependency order. Production seeders create baseline system data only. Test seeders create realistic datasets for development, testing, and QA environments.
14.1 Seeder Hierarchy and Run Order
Seeder Class

Content Description
Environment

14.2 Seeder Rules
NEVER run TestUserSeeder or any Test*Seeder in production. Gate behind APP_ENV !== production check.
All system lookup records use is_system=1. Application code prevents delete of is_system=1 records.
All seeded passwords use bcrypt hashing. Never store plain text even in seeders.
Run DatabaseSeeder in order: Encryption > Privacy > Plans > Tenants > Roles > Permissions > RolePerm > Admin > Lookups > Categories > InvestTypes > ExchangeRates.
ExchangeRateSeeder inserts today's rates only. Thereafter, a daily scheduled job updates rates from RBI/Fixer.io API.
AdminUserSeeder reads APP_ADMIN_EMAIL and APP_ADMIN_PASSWORD from .env — never hardcode in seeder file.
14.3 Test Data Volume Targets
Scenario
Records
Purpose
Minimum viable test
10 users, 30 expenses each = 300 rows
Feature testing, unit tests
Integration test dataset
50 users, 12 months data = 18,000 rows
API integration tests, pagination testing
Performance baseline
1,000 users, 12 months = 360,000 rows
Index validation, query plan verification
Load test dataset
100,000 users, 12 months = 36M rows
Partition testing, query optimization at scale
Full scale simulation
1,000,000 users — use data generation script
Pre-production capacity planning only
TIP
For large test datasets (1M users), use pt-generate-random-data (Percona) or a custom PHP CLI generator.
Do NOT use Eloquent factories for > 100k records — too slow. Use raw SQL LOAD DATA INFILE for bulk seeding.
Generate Parquet fixture files for S3 archive testing — use Python pyarrow or DuckDB to create test archives.

1. DDD Architecture Overview
The Financial Freedom Planner follows a strict 4-layer Domain-Driven Design architecture. Business logic lives exclusively in the Domain layer. The Presentation layer is thin — controllers validate via Form Requests and delegate to Application Actions immediately.
1.1 Four-Layer Architecture
Layer
Location
Responsibility
Presentation Layer
app/Http/Controllers
app/Http/Resources
routes/
Receives HTTP requests. Delegates immediately to Application layer. Zero business logic. Returns API Resources or Blade views.
Application Layer
src/Domain/{Name}/Actions
src/Domain/{Name}/Services
src/Domain/{Name}/DTOs
Orchestrates use cases. Calls Domain services and repositories. Handles transactions. Dispatches Events. No SQL or HTTP knowledge.
Domain Layer
src/Domain/{Name}/Models
src/Domain/{Name}/Contracts
src/Domain/{Name}/ValueObjects
src/Domain/{Name}/Events
Pure business logic. Domain Models, Value Objects, Domain Events, Repository Contracts (interfaces). Zero framework dependency.
Infrastructure Layer
src/Domain/{Name}/Repositories
app/Jobs
app/Listeners
app/Notifications
Implements Domain Contracts. Eloquent repositories, queue jobs, external APIs, file storage. Framework-dependent but domain-decoupled.
1.2 DDD Principles Applied
Principle
Implementation in this Project
Ubiquitous Language
Every class, method, variable uses domain terminology. "GoalContribution" not "GoalPayment". "EmergencyFundDeposit" not "FundAdd".
Bounded Contexts
12 domains are isolated. Income domain knows nothing about Investment domain. Cross-domain communication via Events or Application Services only.
Dependency Inversion
Domain layer defines Repository interfaces (Contracts). Infrastructure layer implements them. Domain never imports Eloquent directly.
Value Objects
Money amounts wrapped in Money value object. Immutable. BCMath arithmetic inside. Prevents raw float usage across the codebase.
Domain Events
State changes dispatch Domain Events (GoalMilestoneReached, BudgetExceeded). Listeners handle side effects (notifications, cache, audit).
Aggregate Roots
FinancialGoal is an aggregate root — owns GoalContributions. SavingAccount owns SavingTransactions. Debt owns AmortizationSchedule.
Repository Pattern
All data access through Repository interfaces. Application layer is testable without DB. Infrastructure swappable (e.g., from Eloquent to Doctrine).
CQRS (Soft)
Read models (financial_snapshots, expense_trends) are separate from write models. Dashboard reads from snapshots, not live aggregate queries.
1.3 Request Lifecycle
FLOW
HTTP Request  ->  Route  ->  Middleware (Auth, Tenant, RateLimit, Idempotency)
  ->  FormRequest (validation)  ->  Controller (thin — 5 lines max)
  ->  Action (use-case orchestrator)  ->  Service (domain logic)
  ->  Repository (data access)  ->  Model (Eloquent)
  ->  Domain Event dispatched  ->  Listeners (notifications, cache, audit)
  ->  API Resource (response formatting)  ->  HTTP Response
2. Root Project Structure
The project separates Laravel framework concerns (app/) from domain business logic (src/Domain/). This allows the Domain layer to be framework-agnostic and independently testable.
financial-freedom-planner/
|
|-- app/                              # Laravel Application Layer
|   |-- Console/                      # Artisan commands
|   |-- Exceptions/                   # Exception handlers
|   |-- Http/
|   |   |-- Controllers/              # Thin HTTP controllers (API + Web)
|   |   |-- Middleware/               # HTTP middleware stack
|   |   |-- Requests/                 # Form Request validation classes
|   |   |-- Resources/               # API Resource transformers
|   |-- Jobs/                         # Queue jobs (report gen, XIRR, etc.)
|   |-- Listeners/                    # Event listeners (notifications, cache)
|   |-- Notifications/               # Laravel notification classes
|   |-- Policies/                     # Authorization policies
|   |-- Providers/                    # Service providers
|
|-- src/                              # Domain Layer (DDD core)
|   |-- Domain/                       # All bounded contexts live here
|   |   |-- Auth/                     # Authentication domain
|   |   |-- Income/                   # Salary & income domain
|   |   |-- Expense/                  # Expense tracking domain
|   |   |-- Savings/                  # Savings management domain
|   |   |-- EmergencyFund/            # Emergency fund domain
|   |   |-- Goal/                     # Financial goals domain
|   |   |-- Investment/               # Investment tracking domain
|   |   |-- Debt/                     # Debt management domain
|   |   |-- Report/                   # Reports & analytics domain
|   |   |-- Notification/             # Notification management domain
|   |   |-- Dashboard/               # Dashboard aggregation domain
|   |   |-- SharedKernel/            # Shared DDD building blocks
|
|-- database/
|   |-- migrations/                   # 58 ordered migrations
|   |-- seeders/                      # 23 seeders (prod + test)
|   |-- factories/                    # Eloquent model factories
|
|-- routes/
|   |-- api.php                       # All API routes (v1)
|   |-- web.php                       # Blade web routes
|   |-- auth.php                      # Auth-specific routes
|   |-- admin.php                     # Admin-only routes
|   |-- channels.php                  # Broadcast channels
|
|-- config/                            # All configuration files
|-- resources/                        # Blade views, JS, CSS
|-- storage/                          # Logs, cache, compiled files
|-- tests/                            # PHPUnit / Pest tests
|   |-- Unit/                         # Domain logic unit tests
|   |-- Feature/                      # API feature tests
|   |-- Integration/                  # Repository integration tests
|
|-- .env.example                      # Environment template
|-- composer.json                     # PHP dependencies
|-- phpunit.xml                       # Test configuration
`-- README.md                         # Project documentation
3. Domain Folder Template
Every bounded domain follows this identical folder structure. Consistency across domains means any developer can navigate any domain immediately. The structure enforces DDD layer separation at the filesystem level.
src/Domain/{DomainName}/
|
|-- Actions/                          # Use-case orchestrators (1 class = 1 use case)
|   |-- Create{Entity}Action.php      # e.g. CreateIncomeEntryAction.php
|   |-- Update{Entity}Action.php
|   |-- Delete{Entity}Action.php
|   `-- {SpecificUseCase}Action.php   # e.g. RecordSipTransactionAction.php
|
|-- Contracts/                        # Repository interfaces (no Eloquent here)
|   |-- {Entity}RepositoryInterface.php
|   `-- {Entity}ReadRepositoryInterface.php   # Separate read model contract
|
|-- DTOs/                             # Data Transfer Objects (typed input/output)
|   |-- {Entity}Data.php              # Input DTO from FormRequest
|   `-- {Entity}SummaryData.php       # Output DTO for API Resources
|
|-- Events/                           # Domain events
|   |-- {Entity}Created.php
|   |-- {Entity}Updated.php
|   `-- {DomainEvent}Occurred.php    # e.g. BudgetExceeded.php
|
|-- Exceptions/                       # Domain-specific exceptions
|   |-- {Entity}NotFoundException.php
|   `-- {DomainRule}ViolationException.php   # e.g. InsufficientFundsException.php
|
|-- Models/                           # Eloquent models (domain models)
|   |-- {Entity}.php                  # Primary entity model
|   `-- {RelatedEntity}.php
|
|-- Repositories/                     # Eloquent implementations of Contracts
|   |-- Eloquent{Entity}Repository.php
|   `-- Eloquent{Entity}ReadRepository.php
|
|-- Services/                         # Domain services (complex business logic)
|   |-- {DomainName}Service.php       # Primary domain service
|   `-- {Calculation}Service.php      # e.g. GoalProjectionService.php
|
|-- ValueObjects/                     # Immutable domain value types
|   |-- Money.php                     # BCMath-backed monetary value
|   |-- Percentage.php
|   `-- DateRange.php
|
`-- Enums/                            # PHP 8.1+ backed enums
    |-- {Entity}StatusEnum.php        # e.g. GoalStatusEnum.php
    `-- {CategoryType}Enum.php
3.1 Folder Responsibility Map
File / Class
Responsibility
Actions/
Single-responsibility use-case classes. Called by Controllers. Orchestrate Services and Repositories. Wrap in DB transactions where needed.
Contracts/
PHP interfaces for repositories. Domain layer depends on these — never on Eloquent directly. Enables swapping storage implementations.
DTOs/
Typed data transfer objects. FormRequests create Input DTOs. Actions return Output DTOs. No raw arrays passed between layers.
Events/
Immutable domain events dispatched when state changes. Carry the minimum data needed by listeners. Named in past tense: BudgetExceeded.
Exceptions/
Business rule violations as typed exceptions. Caught by exception handler and converted to HTTP responses. DomainException base class.
Models/
Eloquent models with no business logic inside them. Only relationships, casts, scopes, and fillable. Logic lives in Services.
Repositories/
Eloquent implementations of Contract interfaces. All SQL queries live here. No SQL anywhere else in the application.
Services/
Complex domain calculations and business rules. Stateless. Injected into Actions. e.g. GoalProjectionService, XirrCalculationService.
ValueObjects/
Immutable typed wrappers. Money wraps BCMath. Prevents primitive obsession. Two Money instances are equal if same amount + currency.
Enums/
PHP 8.1+ backed enums for status fields, type classifications. Replaces magic string constants across the codebase.

Complete file tree for all 12 bounded domains. Every domain follows the identical template from Section 3. File names use the exact domain language — no generic names like "Manager" or "Handler".

5. HTTP Layer — Controllers, Requests, Resources
5.1 Controllers
All controllers are thin — maximum 5-7 lines per method. Every controller method: validates via FormRequest, creates DTO, calls one Action, returns API Resource. No business logic. No direct model access.

6. Middleware
app/Http/Middleware/
|-- Auth/
|   |-- Authenticate.php                    # Sanctum token validation
|   |-- RedirectIfAuthenticated.php
|   `-- EnsureEmailIsVerified.php
|-- Tenant/
|   |-- ResolveTenant.php                   # Subdomain -> Tenant lookup -> bind to request
|   `-- EnsureTenantIsActive.php
|-- Security/
|   |-- IdempotencyMiddleware.php           # Check/store Idempotency-Key header
|   |-- RateLimitByTier.php                 # Tiered rate limits by route group
|   |-- SecurityHeaders.php                 # X-Frame-Options, CSP, etc.
|   |-- SanitizeInput.php                   # Strip unexpected input characters
|   `-- VerifySignedUrl.php                 # For email verification links
|-- Privacy/
|   |-- RequireConsent.php                  # DPDP consent check on data routes
|   `-- NoCacheFinancialData.php            # Cache-Control: no-store on financial APIs
|-- Admin/
|   |-- RequireAdminRole.php
|   `-- AdminIpAllowlist.php                # IP allowlist for admin endpoints
`-- Logging/
    `-- StructuredRequestLogger.php         # JSON request/response logging with X-Request-ID
6.1 Middleware Responsibilities
File / Class
Responsibility
ResolveTenant.php
Reads subdomain from Host header. Looks up tenant in cache then DB. Binds Tenant to request. Returns 404 if tenant not found or inactive.
IdempotencyMiddleware.php
Reads Idempotency-Key header. Checks idempotency_keys table. If found and valid: return cached response. If missing: return 400 on mutation endpoints.
RateLimitByTier.php
Applies different rate limits per route group: Auth=5/min, Financial writes=30/min, Reports=3/min, Bulk=10/hr. Uses Redis for counters.
SecurityHeaders.php
Adds: X-Frame-Options: DENY, X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff, Referrer-Policy, Permissions-Policy. Applied to all responses.
NoCacheFinancialData.php
Adds Cache-Control: no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate to all financial data API responses. Prevents browser and CDN caching.
RequireConsent.php
Checks consent_records for data_processing consent before allowing financial data routes. Returns 403 with consent_required message if withdrawn.
AdminIpAllowlist.php
Reads ADMIN_ALLOWED_IPS from config. Returns 403 if request IP not in allowlist. Applied to all /api/v1/admin/* routes.
StructuredRequestLogger.php
Logs every request as structured JSON: {request_id, user_id, tenant_id, method, path, status, duration_ms}. Masks PII fields (email, phone, amounts).
6.2 Middleware Stack Order
ORDER
Global (all requests): StructuredRequestLogger -> SecurityHeaders -> NoCacheFinancialData
API routes: ResolveTenant -> EnsureTenantIsActive -> Authenticate -> EnsureEmailIsVerified
Financial mutation routes: + IdempotencyMiddleware -> RateLimitByTier -> RequireConsent
Admin routes: + RequireAdminRole -> AdminIpAllowlist
Auth routes only: + RateLimitByTier (5/min) [no Authenticate middleware]
7. Policies
One Policy per Domain Model. Every FormRequest authorize() method delegates to its Policy. Policies enforce both authentication (resource ownership) and authorization (role/permission checks). No inline auth checks in controllers.
app/Policies/
|-- SalarySourcePolicy.php
|-- IncomeEntryPolicy.php
|-- ExpensePolicy.php
|-- ExpenseCategoryPolicy.php
|-- ExpenseBudgetPolicy.php
|-- SavingAccountPolicy.php
|-- SavingTransactionPolicy.php
|-- EmergencyFundPolicy.php
|-- FinancialGoalPolicy.php
|-- GoalContributionPolicy.php
|-- InvestmentPolicy.php
|-- InvestmentTransactionPolicy.php
|-- SipSchedulePolicy.php
|-- DebtPolicy.php
|-- DebtPaymentPolicy.php
|-- NotificationPolicy.php
|-- UserPolicy.php              # Admin: manage all users
`-- AdminPolicy.php             # Admin-only operations gate
7.1 Key Policy Rules
File / Class
Responsibility
SalarySourcePolicy
view/create: authenticated user. update/delete: user_id === auth user. viewAny: own sources only.
ExpensePolicy
view/update/delete: expense.user_id === auth.id. create: any authenticated user. Cross-user access returns 403.
ExpenseCategoryPolicy
view: auth user (own + system). update/delete: own categories only. delete: reject if is_system=true.
FinancialGoalPolicy
All methods: goal.user_id === auth.id. contribute: goal must be status=active (not paused/cancelled).
InvestmentPolicy
view/update/delete: investment.user_id === auth.id. Explicit check prevents BOLA via ULID guessing.
DebtPolicy
All CRUD: debt.user_id === auth.id. recordPayment: debt.status !== closed (DebtAlreadyClosedException).
UserPolicy
viewAny/update/delete: only admin role. update: cannot demote last admin. delete: cannot delete own account via admin panel.
AdminPolicy
Gate for admin panel access. Checks user has admin role AND request IP is in admin allowlist.
8. Jobs (Queue Workers)
Jobs handle all async, long-running, and scheduled tasks. They run on dedicated queue workers (Laravel Horizon). Never run jobs synchronously in the request path — always dispatch to queue.
app/Jobs/
|-- Income/
|   `-- SyncRecurringIncomeJob.php         # Monthly: auto-create recurring income entries
|-- Report/
|   |-- GenerateMonthlyReportJob.php        # Async report generation (queued)
|   |-- GenerateQuarterlyReportJob.php
|   |-- GenerateYearlyReportJob.php
|   |-- GenerateTaxReportJob.php
|   |-- ExportReportPdfJob.php
|   `-- ExportReportExcelJob.php
|-- Investment/
|   |-- ComputeXirrForInvestmentJob.php    # Nightly: Newton-Raphson XIRR per investment
|   |-- ComputeCagrForInvestmentJob.php
|   `-- ExecuteSipInstallmentJob.php        # Daily: process due SIP schedules
|-- Snapshot/
|   |-- GenerateMonthlySnapshotJob.php      # 1st of month: capture all user balances
|   `-- BackfillSnapshotsJob.php            # Admin: regenerate missing snapshots
|-- Analytics/
|   |-- ComputeExpenseTrendsJob.php         # Nightly: rolling avg + anomaly detection
|   `-- ComputeHealthScoresJob.php          # Nightly: health score for all users
|-- Debt/
|   |-- SendEmiReminderJob.php              # 3 days before: EMI due reminder
|   `-- RegenerateAmortizationScheduleJob.php # After prepayment or rate change
|-- Archive/
|   |-- ArchiveOldTransactionsJob.php       # Monthly: move data to S3 Parquet
|   `-- PurgeExpiredSoftDeletesJob.php      # Daily: hard-delete 90-day-old soft deletes
|-- Compliance/
|   |-- ProcessDataDeletionRequestJob.php   # DPDP: execute scheduled user deletion
|   `-- ExportUserDataJob.php               # DPDP: generate data export ZIP
|-- File/
|   `-- ScanUploadForMalwareJob.php         # After upload: ClamAV/AWS scan
|-- Notification/
|   `-- SendPushNotificationJob.php         # FCM/APNs push dispatch
`-- Exchange/
    `-- UpdateExchangeRatesJob.php           # Daily: fetch latest RBI/Fixer rates
8.1 Critical Job Descriptions
File / Class
Responsibility
GenerateMonthlyReportJob
Dispatched by GenerateMonthlyReportAction. Runs on report queue. Generates report, stores in Redis/S3, marks job complete. Controller polls GET /jobs/{id}.
ComputeXirrForInvestmentJob
Dispatched nightly for every active investment with transactions. Reads all investment_transactions ordered by date. Runs Newton-Raphson. Updates investments.xirr_percentage.
GenerateMonthlySnapshotJob
Dispatched 1st of every month at 00:05 IST. Aggregates all user balances. Inserts into financial_snapshots. Powers dashboard net worth chart.
ProcessDataDeletionRequestJob
Dispatched 30 days after deletion request. Soft-deletes all user data. Tags S3 objects. Updates data_deletion_requests.completed_at. Sends confirmation email.
ArchiveOldTransactionsJob
Monthly. Exports transactions > 24 months old to S3 Parquet. Drops MySQL partition. Updates archived_transaction_meta index table.
ExecuteSipInstallmentJob
Daily at 08:00 IST. Reads sip_schedules WHERE next_due_date = today AND is_active=1. Creates investment_transaction for each. Updates next_due_date.
PurgeExpiredSoftDeletesJob
Daily at 02:00 IST. Hard-deletes records WHERE deleted_at < NOW()-90days. Excludes: ledger_entries, consent_records, audit_logs (permanent).
ScanUploadForMalwareJob
Dispatched immediately after file upload. Calls ClamAV socket or AWS GuardDuty API. Sets file_uploads.scan_status = clean|infected|error.
QUEUE
Queue configuration: 4 dedicated queues with separate worker pools.
  default: General async tasks (notifications, cache invalidation)
  reports: Report generation jobs (memory-intensive, longer timeout)
  nightly: XIRR, snapshots, health scores, trends (large batch jobs)
  critical: Data deletion, compliance exports (highest priority, monitored)
9. Events & Listeners
Domain Events carry state changes. Listeners handle side effects. This decouples the core domain logic (did this happen?) from consequences (what do we do about it?). New behavior = new Listener, zero changes to domain code.
9.1 Event to Listener Mapping
Event
Listeners (in order)
UserRegistered
SendWelcomeEmailListener, CreateDefaultExpenseCategoriesListener, RecordAuditLogListener, RecordConsentListener
UserEmailVerified
SendEmailVerifiedNotificationListener, RecordAuditLogListener
UserLoggedIn
UpdateLastLoginAtListener, RecordLoginEventListener, InvalidateDashboardCacheListener
NewDeviceDetected
SendNewDeviceAlertEmailListener, RecordAuditLogListener
LoginFailed
IncrementFailedLoginCountListener, LockAccountIfThresholdReachedListener
PasswordChanged
InvalidateAllUserTokensListener, SendPasswordChangedEmailListener, RecordAuditLogListener
IncomeEntryRecorded
WriteLedgerEntryListener, InvalidateDashboardCacheListener, RecordAuditLogListener
IncomeEntryDeleted
ReverseLedgerEntryListener, InvalidateDashboardCacheListener
ExpenseCreated
WriteLedgerEntryListener, CheckBudgetThresholdListener, InvalidateDashboardCacheListener, RecordAuditLogListener
BudgetWarningThresholdReached
SendBudgetWarningNotificationListener
BudgetExceeded
SendBudgetExceededNotificationListener, RecordAuditLogListener
SavingDepositMade
UpdateSavingAccountBalanceListener, WriteLedgerEntryListener, CheckSavingsMilestoneListener, InvalidateDashboardCacheListener
SavingMilestoneReached
SendSavingsMilestoneNotificationListener
SavingGoalCompleted

EmergencyFundMilestoneReached

GoalCreated

SendGoalMilestoneNotificationListener
GoalCompleted
SendGoalCompletedEmailListener, RecordAuditLogListener
GoalBehindSchedule
SendGoalBehindScheduleNotificationListener
InvestmentAdded
WriteLedgerEntryListener, DispatchXirrComputationListener, RecordAuditLogListener
InvestmentTransactionRecorded
UpdateInvestmentAmountAndUnitsListener, WriteLedgerEntryListener, DispatchXirrComputationListener
SipInstallmentDue
SendSipReminderNotificationListener
InvestmentMaturing
SendInvestmentMaturityAlertListener
DebtAdded
DispatchAmortizationGenerationListener, RecordAuditLogListener
DebtPaymentRecorded
UpdateDebtOutstandingBalanceListener, UpdateAmortizationScheduleListener, WriteLedgerEntryListener, RecordAuditLogListener

11. Models Registry
Every Eloquent model lives in its domain's Models/ folder. Models contain: relationships, casts, scopes, fillable/guarded, and trait declarations ONLY. Zero business logic inside models — all logic in Services and Actions.
RULE
Model rules: No business logic. No complex queries. No HTTP/Request references.
All money columns cast to Money value object via custom Eloquent cast.
All models with financial data have: HasLedgerEntry trait (auto-creates ledger entries on save).
All user-data models have: BelongsToTenant trait (auto-injects tenant_id scope on all queries).

12. Service Providers & Console Commands
12.1 Service Providers
app/Providers/
|-- AppServiceProvider.php              # Singleton bindings, macro registrations
|-- AuthServiceProvider.php            # Policy -> Model mappings
|-- EventServiceProvider.php           # Event -> Listener mappings (all 30+ events)
|-- RouteServiceProvider.php           # API route binding, rate limit definitions
|-- RepositoryServiceProvider.php      # Interface -> Implementation bindings
|-- DomainServiceProvider.php          # Domain Service singleton registrations
`-- TelescopeServiceProvider.php       # Laravel Telescope (staging only)
KEY
RepositoryServiceProvider.php is critical — it binds every Interface -> Implementation.
Example: $this->app->bind(GoalRepositoryInterface::class, EloquentGoalRepository::class)
This allows swapping Eloquent for any other ORM/storage without touching domain code.
DomainServiceProvider registers Services as singletons (stateless, safe to share across requests).

14.2 Route File Responsibilities
File / Class
Responsibility
routes/api.php
All /api/v1/* routes. Versioned prefix. Middleware groups applied per section.
routes/auth.php
Auth-specific routes included from api.php. Keeps auth routes in one place.
routes/admin.php
Admin-only routes. Included from api.php behind RequireAdminRole + AdminIpAllowlist.
routes/web.php
Blade/web routes for login, register pages. SPA fallback route if applicable.
routes/channels.php
Broadcast channels authorization (Laravel Echo + Pusher/Soketi).
VER
API versioning: all routes prefixed with /api/v1/. When v2 launches, /api/v2/ routes in a new file.
v1 routes remain fully functional. No breaking changes to v1 when v2 is introduced.
Controller namespace: App\Http\Controllers\Api\V1\{Domain}\{Controller}

16. Naming Conventions
Consistent naming is a DDD requirement — it enables ubiquitous language across code, docs, and conversations. Every team member should be able to guess a class name from its description and vice versa.
Class Type
Convention + Examples
Actions
Verb + Noun + Action: CreateIncomeEntryAction, RecordDebtPaymentAction, GenerateMonthlyReportAction
Services
Noun + Service: GoalProjectionService, AmortizationService, XirrCalculationService
Repositories
Eloquent + Entity + Repository: EloquentGoalRepository, EloquentDebtPaymentRepository
Contracts
Entity + RepositoryInterface: GoalRepositoryInterface, DebtRepositoryInterface
DTOs
Entity + Data (input) or EntitySummary + Data (output): GoalData, GoalSummaryData
Events
Past tense noun phrase: GoalCompleted, BudgetExceeded, DebtPaymentRecorded
Listeners
Verb + Object + Listener: SendGoalCompletedEmailListener, WriteLedgerEntryListener
Jobs
Verb + Object + Job: ComputeXirrForInvestmentJob, GenerateMonthlyReportJob
Notifications
Noun + Notification: GoalMilestoneNotification, EmiReminderNotification
Controllers
Entity + Controller: IncomeEntryController, AmortizationScheduleController
Requests
Http verb + Entity + Request: StoreExpenseRequest, UpdateGoalRequest
Resources
Entity + Resource/Collection: InvestmentResource, InvestmentCollection
Policies
Entity + Policy: DebtPolicy, FinancialGoalPolicy
Commands
Verb + Object + Command: ComputeHealthScoresCommand, SendEmiRemindersCommand
Exceptions
Noun + Exception: GoalNotFoundException, InsufficientSavingBalanceException
Enums
Entity + StatusEnum or TypeEnum: GoalStatusEnum, AssetClassEnum
ValueObjects
Domain noun: Money, Percentage, FinancialYear, DeviceFingerprint, TenantId
Traits
Has + Feature: HasUlid, HasAuditLog, HasLedgerEntry, BelongsToTenant
RULE
No generic names: No "Manager", "Handler", "Helper", "Util" classes. Every name describes its exact responsibility.
No abbreviations: "GoalContribution" not "GoalContrib". "AmortizationSchedule" not "AmorSched".
Domain language first: use terms from the financial domain, not technical terms. "recordPayment" not "savePayment".
One class per file, one responsibility per class. File name === class name (PSR-4).

1. DDD Architecture Overview
The Financial Freedom Planner follows a strict 4-layer Domain-Driven Design architecture. Business logic lives exclusively in the Domain layer. The Presentation layer is thin — controllers validate via Form Requests and delegate to Application Actions immediately.
1.1 Four-Layer Architecture
Layer
Location
Responsibility
Presentation Layer
app/Http/Controllers
app/Http/Resources
routes/
Receives HTTP requests. Delegates immediately to Application layer. Zero business logic. Returns API Resources or Blade views.
Application Layer
src/Domain/{Name}/Actions
src/Domain/{Name}/Services
src/Domain/{Name}/DTOs
Orchestrates use cases. Calls Domain services and repositories. Handles transactions. Dispatches Events. No SQL or HTTP knowledge.
Domain Layer
src/Domain/{Name}/Models
src/Domain/{Name}/Contracts
src/Domain/{Name}/ValueObjects
src/Domain/{Name}/Events
Pure business logic. Domain Models, Value Objects, Domain Events, Repository Contracts (interfaces). Zero framework dependency.
Infrastructure Layer
src/Domain/{Name}/Repositories
app/Jobs
app/Listeners
app/Notifications
Implements Domain Contracts. Eloquent repositories, queue jobs, external APIs, file storage. Framework-dependent but domain-decoupled.
1.2 DDD Principles Applied
Principle
Implementation in this Project
Ubiquitous Language
Every class, method, variable uses domain terminology. "GoalContribution" not "GoalPayment". "EmergencyFundDeposit" not "FundAdd".
Bounded Contexts
12 domains are isolated. Income domain knows nothing about Investment domain. Cross-domain communication via Events or Application Services only.
Dependency Inversion
Domain layer defines Repository interfaces (Contracts). Infrastructure layer implements them. Domain never imports Eloquent directly.
Value Objects
Money amounts wrapped in Money value object. Immutable. BCMath arithmetic inside. Prevents raw float usage across the codebase.
Domain Events
State changes dispatch Domain Events (GoalMilestoneReached, BudgetExceeded). Listeners handle side effects (notifications, cache, audit).
Aggregate Roots
FinancialGoal is an aggregate root — owns GoalContributions. SavingAccount owns SavingTransactions. Debt owns AmortizationSchedule.
Repository Pattern
All data access through Repository interfaces. Application layer is testable without DB. Infrastructure swappable (e.g., from Eloquent to Doctrine).
CQRS (Soft)
Read models (financial_snapshots, expense_trends) are separate from write models. Dashboard reads from snapshots, not live aggregate queries.
1.3 Request Lifecycle
FLOW
HTTP Request  ->  Route  ->  Middleware (Auth, Tenant, RateLimit, Idempotency)
  ->  FormRequest (validation)  ->  Controller (thin — 5 lines max)
  ->  Action (use-case orchestrator)  ->  Service (domain logic)
  ->  Repository (data access)  ->  Model (Eloquent)
  ->  Domain Event dispatched  ->  Listeners (notifications, cache, audit)
  ->  API Resource (response formatting)  ->  HTTP Response
2. Root Project Structure
The project separates Laravel framework concerns (app/) from domain business logic (src/Domain/). This allows the Domain layer to be framework-agnostic and independently testable.
financial-freedom-planner/
|
|-- app/                              # Laravel Application Layer
|   |-- Console/                      # Artisan commands
|   |-- Exceptions/                   # Exception handlers
|   |-- Http/
|   |   |-- Controllers/              # Thin HTTP controllers (API + Web)
|   |   |-- Middleware/               # HTTP middleware stack
|   |   |-- Requests/                 # Form Request validation classes
|   |   |-- Resources/               # API Resource transformers
|   |-- Jobs/                         # Queue jobs (report gen, XIRR, etc.)
|   |-- Listeners/                    # Event listeners (notifications, cache)
|   |-- Notifications/               # Laravel notification classes
|   |-- Policies/                     # Authorization policies
|   |-- Providers/                    # Service providers
|
|-- src/                              # Domain Layer (DDD core)
|   |-- Domain/                       # All bounded contexts live here
|   |   |-- Auth/                     # Authentication domain
|   |   |-- Income/                   # Salary & income domain
|   |   |-- Expense/                  # Expense tracking domain
|   |   |-- Savings/                  # Savings management domain

|   |   |-- Dashboard/               # Dashboard aggregation domain
|   |   |-- SharedKernel/            # Shared DDD building blocks
|
|-- database/
|   |-- migrations/                   # 58 ordered migrations
|   |-- seeders/                      # 23 seeders (prod + test)
|   |-- factories/                    # Eloquent model factories
|
|-- routes/
|   |-- api.php                       # All API routes (v1)
|   |-- web.php                       # Blade web routes
|   |-- auth.php                      # Auth-specific routes
|   |-- admin.php                     # Admin-only routes
|   |-- channels.php                  # Broadcast channels
|
|-- config/                            # All configuration files
|-- resources/                        # Blade views, JS, CSS
|-- storage/                          # Logs, cache, compiled files
|-- tests/                            # PHPUnit / Pest tests
|   |-- Unit/                         # Domain logic unit tests
|   |-- Feature/                      # API feature tests
|   |-- Integration/                  # Repository integration tests
|
|-- .env.example                      # Environment template
|-- composer.json                     # PHP dependencies
|-- phpunit.xml                       # Test configuration
`-- README.md                         # Project documentation
3. Domain Folder Template
Every bounded domain follows this identical folder structure. Consistency across domains means any developer can navigate any domain immediately. The structure enforces DDD layer separation at the filesystem level.
src/Domain/{DomainName}/
|
|-- Actions/                          # Use-case orchestrators (1 class = 1 use case)
|   |-- Create{Entity}Action.php      # e.g. CreateIncomeEntryAction.php
|   |-- Update{Entity}Action.php
|   |-- Delete{Entity}Action.php
|   `-- {SpecificUseCase}Action.php   # e.g. RecordSipTransactionAction.php
|
|-- Contracts/                        # Repository interfaces (no Eloquent here)
|   |-- {Entity}RepositoryInterface.php
|   `-- {Entity}ReadRepositoryInterface.php   # Separate read model contract
|
|-- DTOs/                             # Data Transfer Objects (typed input/output)
|   |-- {Entity}Data.php              # Input DTO from FormRequest
|   `-- {Entity}SummaryData.php       # Output DTO for API Resources
|
|-- Events/                           # Domain events
|   |-- {Entity}Created.php
|   |-- {Entity}Updated.php
|   `-- {DomainEvent}Occurred.php    # e.g. BudgetExceeded.php
|
|-- Exceptions/                       # Domain-specific exceptions
|   |-- {Entity}NotFoundException.php
|   `-- {DomainRule}ViolationException.php   # e.g. InsufficientFundsException.php
|
|-- Models/                           # Eloquent models (domain models)
|   |-- {Entity}.php                  # Primary entity model
|   `-- {RelatedEntity}.php
|
|-- Repositories/                     # Eloquent implementations of Contracts
|   |-- Eloquent{Entity}Repository.php
|   `-- Eloquent{Entity}ReadRepository.php
|
|-- Services/                         # Domain services (complex business logic)
|   |-- {DomainName}Service.php       # Primary domain service
|   `-- {Calculation}Service.php      # e.g. GoalProjectionService.php
|
|-- ValueObjects/                     # Immutable domain value types
|   |-- Money.php                     # BCMath-backed monetary value
|   |-- Percentage.php
|   `-- DateRange.php
|
`-- Enums/                            # PHP 8.1+ backed enums
    |-- {Entity}StatusEnum.php        # e.g. GoalStatusEnum.php
    `-- {CategoryType}Enum.php
3.1 Folder Responsibility Map
File / Class
Responsibility
Actions/
Single-responsibility use-case classes. Called by Controllers. Orchestrate Services and Repositories. Wrap in DB transactions where needed.
Contracts/
PHP interfaces for repositories. Domain layer depends on these — never on Eloquent directly. Enables swapping storage implementations.
DTOs/
Typed data transfer objects. FormRequests create Input DTOs. Actions return Output DTOs. No raw arrays passed between layers.
Events/
Immutable domain events dispatched when state changes. Carry the minimum data needed by listeners. Named in past tense: BudgetExceeded.
Exceptions/
Business rule violations as typed exceptions. Caught by exception handler and converted to HTTP responses. DomainException base class.
Models/
Eloquent models with no business logic inside them. Only relationships, casts, scopes, and fillable. Logic lives in Services.
Repositories/
Eloquent implementations of Contract interfaces. All SQL queries live here. No SQL anywhere else in the application.
Services/
Complex domain calculations and business rules. Stateless. Injected into Actions. e.g. GoalProjectionService, XirrCalculationService.
ValueObjects/
Immutable typed wrappers. Money wraps BCMath. Prevents primitive obsession. Two Money instances are equal if same amount + currency.
Enums/
PHP 8.1+ backed enums for status fields, type classifications. Replaces magic string constants across the codebase.
4. Domain File Trees
Complete file tree for all 12 bounded domains. Every domain follows the identical template from Section 3. File names use the exact domain language — no generic names like "Manager" or "Handler".

5. HTTP Layer — Controllers, Requests, Resources
5.1 Controllers
All controllers are thin — maximum 5-7 lines per method. Every controller method: validates via FormRequest, creates DTO, calls one Action, returns API Resource. No business logic. No direct model access.

6. Middleware
app/Http/Middleware/
|-- Auth/
|   |-- Authenticate.php                    # Sanctum token validation
|   |-- RedirectIfAuthenticated.php
|   `-- EnsureEmailIsVerified.php
|-- Tenant/
|   |-- ResolveTenant.php                   # Subdomain -> Tenant lookup -> bind to request
|   `-- EnsureTenantIsActive.php
|-- Security/
|   |-- IdempotencyMiddleware.php           # Check/store Idempotency-Key header
|   |-- RateLimitByTier.php                 # Tiered rate limits by route group
|   |-- SecurityHeaders.php                 # X-Frame-Options, CSP, etc.
|   |-- SanitizeInput.php                   # Strip unexpected input characters
|   `-- VerifySignedUrl.php                 # For email verification links
|-- Privacy/
|   |-- RequireConsent.php                  # DPDP consent check on data routes
|   `-- NoCacheFinancialData.php            # Cache-Control: no-store on financial APIs
|-- Admin/
|   |-- RequireAdminRole.php
|   `-- AdminIpAllowlist.php                # IP allowlist for admin endpoints
`-- Logging/
    `-- StructuredRequestLogger.php         # JSON request/response logging with X-Request-ID
6.1 Middleware Responsibilities
File / Class
Responsibility
ResolveTenant.php
Reads subdomain from Host header. Looks up tenant in cache then DB. Binds Tenant to request. Returns 404 if tenant not found or inactive.
IdempotencyMiddleware.php
Reads Idempotency-Key header. Checks idempotency_keys table. If found and valid: return cached response. If missing: return 400 on mutation endpoints.
RateLimitByTier.php
Applies different rate limits per route group: Auth=5/min, Financial writes=30/min, Reports=3/min, Bulk=10/hr. Uses Redis for counters.
SecurityHeaders.php
Adds: X-Frame-Options: DENY, X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff, Referrer-Policy, Permissions-Policy. Applied to all responses.
NoCacheFinancialData.php
Adds Cache-Control: no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate to all financial data API responses. Prevents browser and CDN caching.
RequireConsent.php
Checks consent_records for data_processing consent before allowing financial data routes. Returns 403 with consent_required message if withdrawn.
AdminIpAllowlist.php
Reads ADMIN_ALLOWED_IPS from config. Returns 403 if request IP not in allowlist. Applied to all /api/v1/admin/* routes.
StructuredRequestLogger.php
Logs every request as structured JSON: {request_id, user_id, tenant_id, method, path, status, duration_ms}. Masks PII fields (email, phone, amounts).
6.2 Middleware Stack Order
ORDER
Global (all requests): StructuredRequestLogger -> SecurityHeaders -> NoCacheFinancialData
API routes: ResolveTenant -> EnsureTenantIsActive -> Authenticate -> EnsureEmailIsVerified
Financial mutation routes: + IdempotencyMiddleware -> RateLimitByTier -> RequireConsent
Admin routes: + RequireAdminRole -> AdminIpAllowlist
Auth routes only: + RateLimitByTier (5/min) [no Authenticate middleware]
7. Policies
One Policy per Domain Model. Every FormRequest authorize() method delegates to its Policy. Policies enforce both authentication (resource ownership) and authorization (role/permission checks). No inline auth checks in controllers.
app/Policies/
|-- SalarySourcePolicy.php
|-- IncomeEntryPolicy.php
|-- ExpensePolicy.php
|-- ExpenseCategoryPolicy.php
|-- ExpenseBudgetPolicy.php
|-- SavingAccountPolicy.php
|-- SavingTransactionPolicy.php
|-- EmergencyFundPolicy.php
|-- FinancialGoalPolicy.php
|-- GoalContributionPolicy.php
|-- InvestmentPolicy.php
|-- InvestmentTransactionPolicy.php
|-- SipSchedulePolicy.php
|-- DebtPolicy.php
|-- DebtPaymentPolicy.php
|-- NotificationPolicy.php
|-- UserPolicy.php              # Admin: manage all users
`-- AdminPolicy.php             # Admin-only operations gate
7.1 Key Policy Rules
File / Class
Responsibility
SalarySourcePolicy
view/create: authenticated user. update/delete: user_id === auth user. viewAny: own sources only.
ExpensePolicy
view/update/delete: expense.user_id === auth.id. create: any authenticated user. Cross-user access returns 403.
ExpenseCategoryPolicy
view: auth user (own + system). update/delete: own categories only. delete: reject if is_system=true.
FinancialGoalPolicy
All methods: goal.user_id === auth.id. contribute: goal must be status=active (not paused/cancelled).
InvestmentPolicy
view/update/delete: investment.user_id === auth.id. Explicit check prevents BOLA via ULID guessing.
DebtPolicy
All CRUD: debt.user_id === auth.id. recordPayment: debt.status !== closed (DebtAlreadyClosedException).
UserPolicy
viewAny/update/delete: only admin role. update: cannot demote last admin. delete: cannot delete own account via admin panel.
AdminPolicy
Gate for admin panel access. Checks user has admin role AND request IP is in admin allowlist.
8. Jobs (Queue Workers)
Jobs handle all async, long-running, and scheduled tasks. They run on dedicated queue workers (Laravel Horizon). Never run jobs synchronously in the request path — always dispatch to queue.
app/Jobs/
|-- Income/
|   `-- SyncRecurringIncomeJob.php         # Monthly: auto-create recurring income entries
|-- Report/
|   |-- GenerateMonthlyReportJob.php        # Async report generation (queued)
|   |-- GenerateQuarterlyReportJob.php
|   |-- GenerateYearlyReportJob.php
|   |-- GenerateTaxReportJob.php
|   |-- ExportReportPdfJob.php
|   `-- ExportReportExcelJob.php
|-- Investment/
|   |-- ComputeXirrForInvestmentJob.php    # Nightly: Newton-Raphson XIRR per investment
|   |-- ComputeCagrForInvestmentJob.php
|   `-- ExecuteSipInstallmentJob.php        # Daily: process due SIP schedules
|-- Snapshot/
|   |-- GenerateMonthlySnapshotJob.php      # 1st of month: capture all user balances
|   `-- BackfillSnapshotsJob.php            # Admin: regenerate missing snapshots
|-- Analytics/
|   |-- ComputeExpenseTrendsJob.php         # Nightly: rolling avg + anomaly detection
|   `-- ComputeHealthScoresJob.php          # Nightly: health score for all users
|-- Debt/
|   |-- SendEmiReminderJob.php              # 3 days before: EMI due reminder
|   `-- RegenerateAmortizationScheduleJob.php # After prepayment or rate change
|-- Archive/
|   |-- ArchiveOldTransactionsJob.php       # Monthly: move data to S3 Parquet
|   `-- PurgeExpiredSoftDeletesJob.php      # Daily: hard-delete 90-day-old soft deletes
|-- Compliance/
|   |-- ProcessDataDeletionRequestJob.php   # DPDP: execute scheduled user deletion
|   `-- ExportUserDataJob.php               # DPDP: generate data export ZIP
|-- File/
|   `-- ScanUploadForMalwareJob.php         # After upload: ClamAV/AWS scan
|-- Notification/
|   `-- SendPushNotificationJob.php         # FCM/APNs push dispatch
`-- Exchange/
    `-- UpdateExchangeRatesJob.php           # Daily: fetch latest RBI/Fixer rates
8.1 Critical Job Descriptions
File / Class
Responsibility
GenerateMonthlyReportJob
Dispatched by GenerateMonthlyReportAction. Runs on report queue. Generates report, stores in Redis/S3, marks job complete. Controller polls GET /jobs/{id}.
ComputeXirrForInvestmentJob
Dispatched nightly for every active investment with transactions. Reads all investment_transactions ordered by date. Runs Newton-Raphson. Updates investments.xirr_percentage.
GenerateMonthlySnapshotJob
Dispatched 1st of every month at 00:05 IST. Aggregates all user balances. Inserts into financial_snapshots. Powers dashboard net worth chart.
ProcessDataDeletionRequestJob
Dispatched 30 days after deletion request. Soft-deletes all user data. Tags S3 objects. Updates data_deletion_requests.completed_at. Sends confirmation email.
ArchiveOldTransactionsJob
Monthly. Exports transactions > 24 months old to S3 Parquet. Drops MySQL partition. Updates archived_transaction_meta index table.
ExecuteSipInstallmentJob
Daily at 08:00 IST. Reads sip_schedules WHERE next_due_date = today AND is_active=1. Creates investment_transaction for each. Updates next_due_date.
PurgeExpiredSoftDeletesJob
Daily at 02:00 IST. Hard-deletes records WHERE deleted_at < NOW()-90days. Excludes: ledger_entries, consent_records, audit_logs (permanent).
ScanUploadForMalwareJob
Dispatched immediately after file upload. Calls ClamAV socket or AWS GuardDuty API. Sets file_uploads.scan_status = clean|infected|error.
QUEUE
Queue configuration: 4 dedicated queues with separate worker pools.
  default: General async tasks (notifications, cache invalidation)
  reports: Report generation jobs (memory-intensive, longer timeout)
  nightly: XIRR, snapshots, health scores, trends (large batch jobs)
  critical: Data deletion, compliance exports (highest priority, monitored)
9. Events & Listeners
Domain Events carry state changes. Listeners handle side effects. This decouples the core domain logic (did this happen?) from consequences (what do we do about it?). New behavior = new Listener, zero changes to domain code.
